<div id="review_280303408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280303408" />
    <a title="Mitchii" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808951-mitchii"><img alt="Mitchii" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605348765p2/4808951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280303408?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitchii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitchii" href="/user/show/4808951-mitchii">Mitchii</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250021847" href="/book/show/14759330-foretold">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=auto-favorites">auto-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280303408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8275992621494359099">I felt the series has just started only to realize that it is the final book. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13487029-foretold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Foretold</a> is an amazing way to end an equally amazing series. And just like the other last books I read before, it’s another bittersweet moment for me. I wanted to cry when I turned the page and saw the acknowledgement page; it took me a while before it finally sinks in. It ended. This truly is the last book. Riley and Beck’s journey has now ended. Is it wrong if I wish there’s more? I’m greedy like that. ;)<br/><br/>Riley finall</span>
  <span id="freeText8275992621494359099" style="display:none">I felt the series has just started only to realize that it is the final book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13487029-foretold" rel="nofollow noopener">Foretold</a> is an amazing way to end an equally amazing series. And just like the other last books I read before, it’s another bittersweet moment for me. I wanted to cry when I turned the page and saw the acknowledgement page; it took me a while before it finally sinks in. It ended. This truly is the last book. Riley and Beck’s journey has now ended. Is it wrong if I wish there’s more? I’m greedy like that. ;)<br /><br />Riley finally realized it—she’s in love with Beck. She thought things will change between them, but she thought wrong. Beck pushed her away, again. Beck was scared that if Riley found out the truth of his life he left in Sadlersville she will eventually leave. He already has enough heartbreaks and he doesn’t want to risk it. But he needed to face the demons he left behind. He needs to clear his name so he can move forward. He (with Riley) returned after many years to his hometown for his mother. Riley saw how people talked about him, and she was more surprised when she firsthand saw how cold her mother treated him. Riley got to know more about him and how hard his life in that town. Even though people say bad things about him, she has faith in him. He has been good to her and now it’s time for her to help him out.<br /><br />Things eventually cleared up. He finally untangled himself from that incident but things are just starting. He still doesn’t know how he’ll face Riley after she confessed to him. But before he makes a move, they have to kick another set of demon butts. It seems that the war between heaven and hell is not yet over. And Riley, the girl he loves is not in possession of her soul.<br /><br />I learned so much about Denver Beck here. If he truly exists I definitely will give him a hug for all the things he experienced with his mother. He did have a terrible mother. I would’ve wanted (because I wanted him to be really happy) if he met his father, because that’s one of the things he desire the most. It’s so maddening to know how his mother used the identity of his father to hurt Beck. But Sadie (his mom) did redeem herself and I kinda forgave her (well…just <em>kinda</em>). But if you love Beck before, you will really love him even more, because there’s definitely more to backwoods boy than meets the eye.<br /><br />Here we thought that the kiss they shared in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11987465-forgiven" rel="nofollow noopener">Forgiven</a> will solidify their relationship. But it didn’t, at the end of book three, Beck pushed her again. But Beck got it wrong, she didn’t leave his side, she embraced his past and has huge belief in him. And she loves him. And I wanted to cry again because they finally sort things out. There were so many times I had pulled my hair out of annoyance because of how stubborn these two were. But when things smoothen, aaaah <strong>it so good.</strong> They both tried to make it work. There were instances that they almost let go. But they didn’t (thanks goodness). And this one, gosh I love me backwoods boy:<blockquote><em>“No, pushin’ me away is not the answer. What we have is more than for when things are goin’ right. It’s forever, Riley.” </em>– Beck</blockquote>That made me smile. They have each other and it so good for them. And what I like about it that, sure, they’re together but these characters didn’t change to lovesick couple. But they do change, they matured and that’s what great about this series, the characters have grown up.<br /><br />But it’s not just about Beck and his past. And it’s not only about Beck &amp; Riley. There’s also another round of fallen, demon slaying like the ones in the first three books. If you enjoyed that stuff, you’ll still get a dose of that…and probably more.<br /><br />We know how endings are: some are sad, some are happy. And glad to say this one’s happy. Life indeed for them had come full circle. I’m gonna miss them! Riley! Beck!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8275992621494359099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343607586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13468080770296546820">This and other reviews on <a href='http://marielle-uniquecritiques.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book Thoughts by Marielle!</a><br/><br/><br/>***WARNING: IF YOU HAVE NOT READ ALL OF THE OTHER BOOKS IN THE DEMON TRAPPERS SERIES, THERE WILL BE SPOILERS IN THIS REVIEW. CONSIDER YOURSELF WARNED.<br/><br/><br/>In the United States, Foretold by Jana Oliver comes out in December. However, in the UK, it came out August 2nd. Instead of waiting for the US release date, I decided to order the book all the way from England. That is how much I love The Demon Trappers series. And the last book did not disappoint</span>
  <span id="freeText13468080770296546820" style="display:none">This and other reviews on <a href="http://marielle-uniquecritiques.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Thoughts by Marielle!</a><br /><br /><br />***WARNING: IF YOU HAVE NOT READ ALL OF THE OTHER BOOKS IN THE DEMON TRAPPERS SERIES, THERE WILL BE SPOILERS IN THIS REVIEW. CONSIDER YOURSELF WARNED.<br /><br /><br />In the United States, Foretold by Jana Oliver comes out in December. However, in the UK, it came out August 2nd. Instead of waiting for the US release date, I decided to order the book all the way from England. That is how much I love The Demon Trappers series. And the last book did not disappoint.<br /> <br /> Beck’s mom, Sadie, was dying of cancer. Even though she had always treated Beck like she hated him, he loved her. Unwilling to let her die alone, Beck and Riley go down to Sadlersville, where Beck is treated with such suspicion and cruelty that Riley can’t help but be curious about his past. Discovering his past was not easy, for he kept it well hidden, but even after she discovered the horrible truth, she felt no different about Beck: she loved him. Now he just had to decide how he felt. Oh, and the Fallen angel Sartael is finally making his move against Lucifer and Ori still holds Riley’s soul in his grasp. Could there possibly be a happy ending to such a horrible story? (Horrible as in tragic. Not as in this story is bad quality. It’s actually awesome, amazing, and any other positive words you can come up with. J)<br /><br /> First off, may I just say that this is one of my favorite series? I've always loved the characters, especially Riley and Beck, but in this final installment, I felt that I got closer to both of them. After Beck finally admits to himself that he loves Riley, he becomes adorable. She turns him into a little puppy and it's just so cute. Riley was funny, as always, not a wimp, and could actually take care of herself. She was also smart and capable. A proper heroine. Beck was sweet and awesome and wonderful, as usual. I fell in love with him in this book and I’m sure you will, too.<br /> <br /> I literally could not stop reading this book. I went over to my friend’s house and brought it with me. I stayed up until 4 o’clock in the morning reading it. It was so captivating that I felt like I couldn’t breathe when I wasn’t reading it (and sometimes even when I was). I didn’t know what was going to happen next and I was so wrapped up in their world that I pretty much stopped living for the two days I read this.<br /><br /> This was an epic love story. There was no insta-love; it took its sweet time. It took four books before they finally fell in love, but it was so worth it. It was unlike any book I have ever read and amazing is the only word coming to my mind. I cannot say anymore on this subject. This book emotionally drained me because…<br /><br /> THIS WAS THE LAST FREAKING BOOK. *cries out of sadness, but also joy* What am I going to do with my life now? I really loved the ending and it was adorable (this is why I am crying with joy. The ending made me really happy, but the fact that it was the ending didn’t), but I DON’T WANT THIS STORY TO END. IT CAN’T!! I couldn’t read for the rest of the day because I was so distraught and I had to find something to do and, of course, this was the day that there was literally nothing to do. I can’t say anymore on this subject except for READ THIS SERIES. READ IT NOW AND ENJOY YOUR TIME WITH IT BECAUSE IT WON’T LAST FOREVER. *cries some more*</span>

<div id="review_383516727" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/383516727" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/383516727?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mitch by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer383516727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3367444759720347901">I don't want to be that devil character perched on the left shoulder whispering bad thoughts, but <i>Foretold</i> is forcing me into the role. I'm sorry, but the first half didn't do it for me, was putting me to sleep - literally. I don't know what I expected from Beck's backstory, but it wasn't this middling bad boy with an abusive mother excuse I got. And the US cover blows the UK cover out of the water, but it doesn't come out until the end of the year.<br/><br/>Actually, that's about it. The second half surp</span>
  <span id="freeText3367444759720347901" style="display:none">I don't want to be that devil character perched on the left shoulder whispering bad thoughts, but <i>Foretold</i> is forcing me into the role. I'm sorry, but the first half didn't do it for me, was putting me to sleep - literally. I don't know what I expected from Beck's backstory, but it wasn't this middling bad boy with an abusive mother excuse I got. And the US cover blows the UK cover out of the water, but it doesn't come out until the end of the year.<br><br>Actually, that's about it. The second half surprised me by being really good; things pick up the minute Riley leaves small town Georgia, so much so I felt I was reading a totally different book. But, that only increases my annoyance at Oliver's decision to hit the pause button while Riley takes time off to explore Beck's past. It's not like we're breaking new ground here either, this isn't the first - nor I suspect the last - time an author has decided to use the troubled childhood thanks to abusive parent excuse to justify the love interest's assery and badassery. At this point, this trope has to be really well done before I feel anything other than boredom, and it’s not here. Sadie isn't for me any more than your basic cruel just because parent who does some malicious things to her kid; I kept expecting some complexity to her character and she didn't do anything besides fit neatly into the nasty parent just because mold.<br><br>As for Beck himself, umm, the reason he's so hated in town, accused of murdering two boys, yeah, somehow that ended up one of the dumbest things I've ever read. How not only he but Riley can fall for the real killer's ruse like that is beyond me. Normally, I don't do pictures, but when even the characters themselves are thinking, hmm, what an odd way to set up a meeting and then merrily go on their way, I ... just ... can't ... resist.<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386352i/745812.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>If that wasn't bad enough, the killer's motive? Lame. How did the cops not catch that when a reporter can explain it without even taking a breath? Honestly, the entirety of the first fifty percent of this book is just a morass of stupidity and complete waste of time filled with laughably underdeveloped new characters combined into a torture I wouldn't wish on my worst enemy.<br><br>The only reason <i>Foretold</i> isn't being filed into the first things I hope to forget in case I ever get amnesia category is because the second half's much improved. The plot's actually interesting as the civil war in Hell comes back to the forefront. There are some genuinely fiendish scenes, mostly involving Lucifer. Characters I'm interested in, like Peter, Ori, Blaze, where have they been, replace those sorry excuses for characters who populate the first half, even if many other returning characters feel more like name checks or cameos. The writing, heck the story generally, feels like an urban fantasy again instead of a bad <i>Sookie Stackhouse</i> knockoff. There's plenty of action, twists and turns that though a little rushed lead the major characters to pretty good, if a little draggy, resolutions.<br><br>I don't know what possessed Oliver to write the first half of this book. I'm sorry, it sucked. At least she doesn't spend the whole book on that detour and I'm happy to say this series ends, if a little late, on a higher note. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3367444759720347901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_308609952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308609952" />
    <a title="Navdha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5491368-navdha"><img alt="Navdha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348070166p2/5491368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308609952?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navdha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navdha" href="/user/show/5491368-navdha">Navdha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=not-very-happy">not-very-happy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=why-oh-why">why-oh-why</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=yay-it-s-over">yay-it-s-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=not-what-i-expected">not-what-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=should-i-even-bother">should-i-even-bother</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=it-was-okay-ish">it-was-okay-ish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308609952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12127407663518741609">Let’s settle for the rating first. 3 stars. The beginning was yawn-worthy but the end chapters did compensate somewhat for the disappointment that were the initial chapters. At least it’s not a grudging 3 stars. <br/><br/>The initial trip to Sadlersville turned out to be eventful. It wasn’t exciting but a closure to Beck’s line of story. It felt forced. I don’t think the Beck we knew since the past three books could be so easily fooled. There were no alarming bells in his head or anything. He acted dumb a</span>
  <span id="freeText12127407663518741609" style="display:none">Let’s settle for the rating first. 3 stars. The beginning was yawn-worthy but the end chapters did compensate somewhat for the disappointment that were the initial chapters. At least it’s not a grudging 3 stars. <br /><br />The initial trip to Sadlersville turned out to be eventful. It wasn’t exciting but a closure to Beck’s line of story. It felt forced. I don’t think the Beck we knew since the past three books could be so easily fooled. There were no alarming bells in his head or anything. He acted dumb and that’s not Beck. It felt like a necessity that had to be settled so that the readers could find out the real killer in a very bland way. <br /><br />Things grew slow with Ori’s return and all his planning. I had been excited to see Riley and Beck finally getting it together but it was, again to my disappointment, boring. I was hoping that when they’d finally do it, I would be more like, “Yaaaay!! They’re doing it! They’re finally doing iiiiittt!!”, but my response was more like, “so yeah, they did it.” I was expecting more bling and bang and it was so damn neutral. I have read scenes where a hug seemed more sensual and intimate than their sex scenes. Such a shame. :(<br /><br />Everything was so dull after they got together. Only the last chapters and the final showdown made me feel like I was actually reading the work of the same author. Oliver mentioned that she had to finish the final installment in a hurry and it showed. Big time. There were so many missing prepositions and those that were used were all in the wrong places. There were too many mistakes to be easily ignored. <br /><i>Dear Editor, you had one job and you screwed it. </i><br />Every chapter started with a header of beautiful wings and ironically they had a typo for “flying”. It's not even funny. <br /><br />Usually I’m the one who complains about authors leaving loose ends in the end of a series but here, some felt so unnecessary; like why did Alan get a part in any of this? Why was it important to include <i>Demonland’s</i> cast? <br />To add to it, Ori’s final sacrifice failed to impress me. The whole deal with Beck and his trip to hell and back, seemed off. The whole showdown could use more build-up and better description. It seemed too easy and it was all over in a matter of lines. On retrospect, I feel like taking back one more star or maybe half…. *sigh* I’ll just wrap it up then.<br /><br />I can’t really say that this series could have been better off as a trilogy. Some matters had to be resolved, like Riley’s soul and Sartael being undead and Ori still being Lucifer's slave and Beck’s past but, it was all so unappealing to me. I don’t even have anything to say about Riley or any other character. I don’t even feel like criticizing a lot. It could have been soooooooooo much better and lively and action packed. It failed to impress me on all levels. I’m really tempted to take back my star now. But I'll resist.... aaaaaannnd it’s over folks. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12127407663518741609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_436329135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436329135" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3946087-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410633472p2/3946087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436329135?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/3946087-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250021847" href="/book/show/14759330-foretold">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3946087-jamie?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436329135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9868057130249337606">I should've known I wouldn't be able to put the book down until I finished. Gosh. All the emotions. Review to come..<br/><br/><b>[Update]</b><br/><br/>If there was anything I had to say about this series as a whole, it’d have to be just how riveting and consistent each book has been. The last and final book of the series, <i>Foretold</i>, was no different. <i>Except</i>… there was something that truly stood out in this instalment – something different that made me appreciate the characters of Riley and Beck and the others I’ve felt so </span>
  <span id="freeText9868057130249337606" style="display:none">I should've known I wouldn't be able to put the book down until I finished. Gosh. All the emotions. Review to come..<br /><br /><b>[Update]</b><br /><br />If there was anything I had to say about this series as a whole, it’d have to be just how riveting and consistent each book has been. The last and final book of the series, <i>Foretold</i>, was no different. <i>Except</i>… there was something that truly stood out in this instalment – something different that made me appreciate the characters of Riley and Beck and the others I’ve felt so connected to so much more. <br /><br /><i>Foretold</i> was a whole new level of intensity, with the final battle finally at hand and the countless lives sure to be lost, I thought Riley and Beck had so much more to lose, on top of all the things that they’ve already lost. It was such a thrilling, suspenseful experience as a reader, trying to get through a book filled with chaos with the faintest slight of hope for the characters you’ve grown so attached to.<br /><br />The most distinctive aspect about the final book was the plot. Essentially, there were two major stories taking place, and I was unsurprisingly immersed in both. The first, being Beck’s personal journey coming to terms with his past and facing his deepest, darkest secrets was… well, completely different from the ‘Demon Trapping’ atmosphere I’ve been so used to. It was lovely. Emotional. Everything I did not expect from an arrogant, tough, frustrating guy like Beck.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[That whole story with Beck heading back to his small hometown with Riley felt a tad bit like <a href="http://www.horrorphile.net/images/the-texas-chainsaw-massacre-2003-jessica-biel-heat1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">Texas Chainsaw Massacre</a>. Okay maybe more than a tad. I don’t know. Let’s just say it was creepy, yet entertaining as heck. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As always, Riley Blackthorne kicked ass. I don’t how else to properly explain her tremendous growth as a character, whilst still remaining true to herself – feisty, confident (the good kind), and completely flawed yet admirable in so many ways.<br /><br />What I treasured in Oliver’s writing was how compelling and satisfying this conclusion was to the series. From the battle between Lucifer and Hell’s rebels <s>haha sounds like a motorcycle gang</s>, to Beck and Riley’s forever-frustrating relationship, and even Simon’s story – I felt Oliver wrapped this series beautifully and truthfully.<br /><br /><i>Foretold</i> was a bittersweet conclusion to such an amazing series of books, and I am glad to have read and experienced it along with the characters I’ve grown so fond of.<br /><br /><b>*Full review taken from <a href="http://missbookaholic.wordpress.com/2013/01/10/foretold-by-jana-oliver/" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Bookaholic</a>!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9868057130249337606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NQ7AlR5PUuvZahkKRp6Fysf1GrZG/oIJDqPpnDIS3APzDg9yb5YmKqu7Y4cI0wvcayTa0rDE7iyBIXMh8qRVbw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7vOpVlv+pAVQiXY2REp5DZwdgiGkOuKQEwOaMHGe/w0o82axKifQxCJYDLsKB/cbMMxCRVIAjrWcgQCNsSh2YQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14743012278985796621">Jana Oliver is an international and Amazon bestselling author who lives in Portugal.<br/><br/>Her novels have won numerous awards, including the Prism Award, the Daphne du Maurier Award for Excellence in Mystery and Supense as well as the National Readers' Choice Award. <br/><br/>Her books include The Demon Trappers Series and Briar Rose (Young Adult), time travel/historical mystery (The Time Rovers Series) and paran</span>
  <span id="freeText14743012278985796621" style="display:none">Jana Oliver is an international and Amazon bestselling author who lives in Portugal.<br /><br />Her novels have won numerous awards, including the Prism Award, the Daphne du Maurier Award for Excellence in Mystery and Supense as well as the National Readers' Choice Award. <br /><br />Her books include The Demon Trappers Series and Briar Rose (Young Adult), time travel/historical mystery (The Time Rovers Series) and paranormal romance (Tangled Souls).<br /><br />She is co-author of Socially Engaged: The Author's Guide to Social media, written with Tyra Burton.<br /><br />She is happiest when she's researching urban legends, peering at old maps and adding to her growing collection of port and Portuguese wines. <br /><br /><br /></span>
